Free Republic Browse ¬∑ Search Bloggers & Personal Topics ¬∑ Post Article FreeRepublic, LLC, PO BOX 9771, FRESNO, CA 93794 FreeRepublic.com is powered by software copyright 2000-2008 John Robinson When reached for comment, the White House referred to recent statements made by press secretary Karoline Leavitt. ‚ÄúThe president does not support American workers being replaced,‚Äù Leavitt told a group of reporters earlier in November. ‚ÄúThe president has a very nuanced, common-sense opinion on this issue ‚Ä¶ but ultimately [he] wants to see American workers in those jobs‚Ä¶ There‚Äôs been a lot of misunderstanding of the president‚Äôs position.‚Äù ‚ÄòDisillusioned‚Äô Public data suggests that many American engineers are being passed over for foreign workers. Throughout 2025, major technology companies such as Microsoft, Meta, Amazon and Intel underwent layoffs ‚Äî continuing what has been a years-long trend in the industry. The workers interviewed by the DCNF were not employed at these specific tech companies. Roughly 428,000 tech workers lost their job between 2022 and 2023, and a total of 384 tech companies handed pink slips to roughly 124,000 workers in 2024, according to the Institute for Sound Public Policy (ISPP). While H-1Bs have an outsized influence on the tech world, workers across all major industries are impacted by imported foreign labor. The flow of H-1B workers into the U.S. has largely kept apace despite these mass layoffs, with the ISPP finding that the number of H-1B visa workers has grown 80% since the Great Recession low in 2011. Experts estimate that nearly 660,000 H-1B workers were living in the U.S. in October 2024. Established by Congress in 1990, the H-1B program was originally intended to utilize ‚Äúhighly specialized‚Äù foreign labor, according to the U.S. Citizenship and Immigration Services. Although it‚Äôs a nonimmigrant visa, H-1B holders can eventually become eligible to apply for legal permanent residence, allowing them to stay in the country indefinitely. The tech industry dominates the use of H-1Bs, with tech companies accounting for nearly 70% of H-1B petitions annually, according to Nation Connections, a site dedicated to helping individuals navigate immigration laws in different countries. Other American-born tech workers have shared similar experiences to Jonathan‚Äôs, and have stayed silent due to fear of retaliation. ‚ÄúI do feel kind of disillusioned with the industry,‚Äù said Riley, who graduated with a software engineering degree in 2021. ‚ÄúSoftware engineers have a higher unemployment rate right now than art history majors.‚Äù Art history majors have a 3% unemployment rate, according to the Federal Reserve Bank of New York, which compiled data released in February. Computer engineering majors, on the other hand, currently suffer from a 7.5% unemployment rate. Riley said he noticed a monumental shift in the hiring practices of an Austin-based company he worked at for several years. He claims the company ‚Äî which had faced consistent complaints from engineers about pay ‚Äî increasingly staffed its engineering departments with employees from South America and eventually established an office in Colombia to better utilize the continent‚Äôs workforce. ‚ÄúI believe that that was done in order to, you know, reduce their labor costs so that they could get engineers without negotiating with [the American-born engineers] or caving to their demands,‚Äù Riley said. Jonathan described a similar situation after the California-based company he worked for introduced an India development center. Roughly six months after the center was launched, he said the company stopped hiring outside of India altogether. About a year after he left, Jonathan‚Äôs former coworker informed him that around half of the company‚Äôs security personnel was let go. ‚ÄúYou‚Äôre going to lose advancement opportunities, you‚Äôre going to have HR problems and you‚Äôre going to be not a team player if you don‚Äôt advocate with open arms the idea of an Indian development center being opened up to your company or a billion H-1Bs flooding the market,‚Äù Jonathan said about the situation he was facing and the continued pressure to not speak out. ‚ÄòWe‚Äôre All In The Process Of Being Replaced‚Äô India stands far above any other nation as the top source of foreign labor, making up 72% of all H-1B recipients between October 2022 and September 2023, per a March 2024 report from the Department of Homeland Security. ‚ÄúWe‚Äôre all in the process of being replaced,‚Äù John, who worked for an insurance company in Connecticut, told the DCNF. John said there were around 350 IT employees ‚Äî all purportedly American ‚Äî at his company when he first began in 2006. Throughout his decade at the company, he claims they were all steadily booted out in favor of foreign workers. ‚ÄúMost of the time they had them train their Indian replacements before they left as a condition of receiving their severance,‚Äù he told the DCNF. ‚ÄúSo what I saw over a period of time was a whole bunch of lives being destroyed.‚Äù ‚ÄúA lot of the younger kids can‚Äôt find employment,‚Äù John said of the industry. ‚ÄúThey spent a whole bunch of money learning all of this stuff ‚Äî computer programs, cloud platforms, this that the other thing ‚Äî but they can‚Äôt find work.‚Äù The tech employees who spoke to the DCNF are struggling to find work in the U.S. at a time when college debt has skyrocketed to historical highs. Roughly 44 million Americans owe more than $1.7 trillion in student debt, according to the National Conference of State Legislatures. Engineering degrees in general are consistently ranked as one of the costliest to earn. Like his coworkers before him, John was ultimately ‚Äúreplaced‚Äù and handed a severance agreement that forbids him from discussing the matter publicly. ‚ÄúComing home to western Washington from Alaska, I assumed that finding a better-paying job would be no issue ‚Äî we are home to some of the nation‚Äôs largest tech companies,‚Äù Luke Hawthorne told the DCNF. ‚ÄúI spent nearly a year over 2022 and 2023 searching for my current job, a job which pays me about the same as I was making before.‚Äù While Hawthorne still considers himself lucky to be employed, he said his current salary ‚Äúdoesn‚Äôt even approach‚Äù the threshold it takes to afford a home in his area of Washington State. His home state‚Äôs software developer workforce grew by more than 16% through H-1B certifications over just a 9-month period, with 83% of these positions approved at or below Washington State‚Äôs median wage, according to public data he analyzed and shared with the DCNF. ‚ÄúThe ‚Äòbest and brightest‚Äô argument simply doesn‚Äôt square with how the program is being used,‚Äù Hawthorne said. ‚ÄúAnother important aspect of it is that you aren‚Äôt competing just with the new arrivals, but with all of the tech workers who have been replaced ‚Äî I have friends with talent and experience who have been out of work for years.‚Äù Many of the tech workers who spoke to the DCNF have since become involved with U.S. Tech Workers, an advocacy group that highlights the plight of American employees negatively affected by the H-1B program and pushes Washington, D.C., for change. Trump, who has implemented some of the most hawkish immigration policies since returning to office, has appeared to give mixed signals on the issue as major players within his own inner circle disagree over reform. The president‚Äôs coalition appeared fragmented in the weeks leading up to his second presidential inauguration, with business magnate Elon Musk touting H-1Bs in December 2024 and Vivek Ramaswamy suggesting that the U.S. needs foreign talent because American culture ‚Äúvenerated mediocrity over excellence.‚Äù Georgia GOP Rep. Marjorie Taylor Greene, a former a top Trump ally who is resigning from Congress, said in November she would introduce legislation completely phasing out the H-1B program, accusing tech companies of abusing the system at the expense of Americans. Trump initially appeared to side with the pro-H-1B faction, declaring in December 2024 that he was ‚Äúa believer‚Äù in the visa program. In what appeared to be a major shift into the pro-American worker camp, Trump in September signed a proclamation slapping a $100,000 fee on all new H-1B applications, but opponents of the program have criticized the fee‚Äôs limitations and workarounds. Earlier in November, Trump once again publicly touted the need for H-1Bs to import foreign workers. As Washington, D.C., continues to debate the value of H-1Bs, American tech workers say they‚Äôve been left out to dry. ‚ÄúI graduated college seven years ago and I remember in high school them telling us, ‚Äòlearn to code and you‚Äôll have a good job,'‚Äù Joseph Ibrahim, an unemployed tech worker based in Florida, told the DCNF. ‚ÄúWell, it turns out they outsource the coding jobs also, not just the manufacturing jobs.‚Äù Ibrahim got a degree in information systems, business analytics and information systems, but has been struggling to find work since April. Unlike many of the tech workers who spoke to the DCNF, he had no problem being identified by his full name. ‚ÄúWhat are they gonna do?‚Äù Ibrahim asked. ‚ÄúThey‚Äôre already not hiring me.‚Äù ‚ÄúYou know, if I went into college and on the pamphlet, there were like, ‚Äòpros and cons of studying something in computer science: you may have to train your replacement at some point in your career,‚Äô I would have never studied this,‚Äù he said. The president‚Äôs coalition appeared fragmented in the weeks leading up to his second presidential inauguration, with business magnate Elon Musk touting H-1Bs in December 2024 and Vivek Ramaswamy suggesting that the U.S. needs foreign talent because American culture ‚Äúvenerated mediocrity over excellence.‚Äù Georgia GOP Rep. Marjorie Taylor Greene, a former a top Trump ally who is resigning from Congress, said in November she would introduce legislation completely phasing out the H-1B program, accusing tech companies of abusing the system at the expense of Americans. Trump initially appeared to side with the pro-H-1B faction, declaring in December 2024 that he was ‚Äúa believer‚Äù in the visa program. In what appeared to be a major shift into the pro-American worker camp, Trump in September signed a proclamation slapping a $100,000 fee on all new H-1B applications, but opponents of the program have criticized the fee‚Äôs limitations and workarounds. Earlier in November, Trump once again publicly touted the need for H-1Bs to import foreign workers. As Washington, D.C., continues to debate the value of H-1Bs, American tech workers say they‚Äôve been left out to dry. ‚ÄúI graduated college seven years ago and I remember in high school them telling us, ‚Äòlearn to code and you‚Äôll have a good job,'‚Äù Joseph Ibrahim, an unemployed tech worker based in Florida, told the DCNF. ‚ÄúWell, it turns out they outsource the coding jobs also, not just the manufacturing jobs.‚Äù Ibrahim got a degree in information systems, business analytics and information systems, but has been struggling to find work since April. Unlike many of the tech workers who spoke to the DCNF, he had no problem being identified by his full name. ‚ÄúWhat are they gonna do?‚Äù Ibrahim asked. ‚ÄúThey‚Äôre already not hiring me.‚Äù ‚ÄúYou know, if I went into college and on the pamphlet, there were like, ‚Äòpros and cons of studying something in computer science: you may have to train your replacement at some point in your career,‚Äô I would have never studied this,‚Äù he said. Free Republic Browse ¬∑ Search Bloggers & Personal Topics ¬∑ Post Article FreeRepublic, LLC, PO BOX 9771, FRESNO, CA 93794 FreeRepublic.com is powered by software copyright 2000-2008 John Robinson ‚ÄòDisillusioned‚Äô Public data suggests that many American engineers are being passed over for foreign workers. Throughout 2025, major technology companies such as Microsoft, Meta, Amazon and Intel underwent layoffs ‚Äî continuing what has been a years-long trend in the industry. The workers interviewed by the DCNF were not employed at these specific tech companies. Roughly 428,000 tech workers lost their job between 2022 and 2023, and a total of 384 tech companies handed pink slips to roughly 124,000 workers in 2024, according to the Institute for Sound Public Policy (ISPP). While H-1Bs have an outsized influence on the tech world, workers across all major industries are impacted by imported foreign labor. The flow of H-1B workers into the U.S. has largely kept apace despite these mass layoffs, with the ISPP finding that the number of H-1B visa workers has grown 80% since the Great Recession low in 2011. Experts estimate that nearly 660,000 H-1B workers were living in the U.S. in October 2024. Established by Congress in 1990, the H-1B program was originally intended to utilize ‚Äúhighly specialized‚Äù foreign labor, according to the U.S. Citizenship and Immigration Services. Although it‚Äôs a nonimmigrant visa, H-1B holders can eventually become eligible to apply for legal permanent residence, allowing them to stay in the country indefinitely. The tech industry dominates the use of H-1Bs, with tech companies accounting for nearly 70% of H-1B petitions annually, according to Nation Connections, a site dedicated to helping individuals navigate immigration laws in different countries. Other American-born tech workers have shared similar experiences to Jonathan‚Äôs, and have stayed silent due to fear of retaliation. ‚ÄúI do feel kind of disillusioned with the industry,‚Äù said Riley, who graduated with a software engineering degree in 2021. ‚ÄúSoftware engineers have a higher unemployment rate right now than art history majors.‚Äù Art history majors have a 3% unemployment rate, according to the Federal Reserve Bank of New York, which compiled data released in February. Computer engineering majors, on the other hand, currently suffer from a 7.5% unemployment rate. Riley said he noticed a monumental shift in the hiring practices of an Austin-based company he worked at for several years. He claims the company ‚Äî which had faced consistent complaints from engineers about pay ‚Äî increasingly staffed its engineering departments with employees from South America and eventually established an office in Colombia to better utilize the continent‚Äôs workforce. ‚ÄúI believe that that was done in order to, you know, reduce their labor costs so that they could get engineers without negotiating with [the American-born engineers] or caving to their demands,‚Äù Riley said. Jonathan described a similar situation after the California-based company he worked for introduced an India development center. Roughly six months after the center was launched, he said the company stopped hiring outside of India altogether. About a year after he left, Jonathan‚Äôs former coworker informed him that around half of the company‚Äôs security personnel was let go. ‚ÄúYou‚Äôre going to lose advancement opportunities, you‚Äôre going to have HR problems and you‚Äôre going to be not a team player if you don‚Äôt advocate with open arms the idea of an Indian development center being opened up to your company or a billion H-1Bs flooding the market,‚Äù Jonathan said about the situation he was facing and the continued pressure to not speak out. ‚ÄòWe‚Äôre All In The Process Of Being Replaced‚Äô India stands far above any other nation as the top source of foreign labor, making up 72% of all H-1B recipients between October 2022 and September 2023, per a March 2024 report from the Department of Homeland Security. ‚ÄúWe‚Äôre all in the process of being replaced,‚Äù John, who worked for an insurance company in Connecticut, told the DCNF. John said there were around 350 IT employees ‚Äî all purportedly American ‚Äî at his company when he first began in 2006. Throughout his decade at the company, he claims they were all steadily booted out in favor of foreign workers. ‚ÄúMost of the time they had them train their Indian replacements before they left as a condition of receiving their severance,‚Äù he told the DCNF. ‚ÄúSo what I saw over a period of time was a whole bunch of lives being destroyed.‚Äù ‚ÄúA lot of the younger kids can‚Äôt find employment,‚Äù John said of the industry. ‚ÄúThey spent a whole bunch of money learning all of this stuff ‚Äî computer programs, cloud platforms, this that the other thing ‚Äî but they can‚Äôt find work.‚Äù The tech employees who spoke to the DCNF are struggling to find work in the U.S. at a time when college debt has skyrocketed to historical highs. Roughly 44 million Americans owe more than $1.7 trillion in student debt, according to the National Conference of State Legislatures. Engineering degrees in general are consistently ranked as one of the costliest to earn. Like his coworkers before him, John was ultimately ‚Äúreplaced‚Äù and handed a severance agreement that forbids him from discussing the matter publicly. ‚ÄúComing home to western Washington from Alaska, I assumed that finding a better-paying job would be no issue ‚Äî we are home to some of the nation‚Äôs largest tech companies,‚Äù Luke Hawthorne told the DCNF. ‚ÄúI spent nearly a year over 2022 and 2023 searching for my current job, a job which pays me about the same as I was making before.‚Äù While Hawthorne still considers himself lucky to be employed, he said his current salary ‚Äúdoesn‚Äôt even approach‚Äù the threshold it takes to afford a home in his area of Washington State. His home state‚Äôs software developer workforce grew by more than 16% through H-1B certifications over just a 9-month period, with 83% of these positions approved at or below Washington State‚Äôs median wage, according to public data he analyzed and shared with the DCNF. ‚ÄúThe ‚Äòbest and brightest‚Äô argument simply doesn‚Äôt square with how the program is being used,‚Äù Hawthorne said. ‚ÄúAnother important aspect of it is that you aren‚Äôt competing just with the new arrivals, but with all of the tech workers who have been replaced ‚Äî I have friends with talent and experience who have been out of work for years.‚Äù Many of the tech workers who spoke to the DCNF have since become involved with U.S. Tech Workers, an advocacy group that highlights the plight of American employees negatively affected by the H-1B program and pushes Washington, D.C., for change. Trump, who has implemented some of the most hawkish immigration policies since returning to office, has appeared to give mixed signals on the issue as major players within his own inner circle disagree over reform. The president‚Äôs coalition appeared fragmented in the weeks leading up to his second presidential inauguration, with business magnate Elon Musk touting H-1Bs in December 2024 and Vivek Ramaswamy suggesting that the U.S. needs foreign talent because American culture ‚Äúvenerated mediocrity over excellence.‚Äù Georgia GOP Rep. Marjorie Taylor Greene, a former a top Trump ally who is resigning from Congress, said in November she would introduce legislation completely phasing out the H-1B program, accusing tech companies of abusing the system at the expense of Americans. Trump initially appeared to side with the pro-H-1B faction, declaring in December 2024 that he was ‚Äúa believer‚Äù in the visa program. In what appeared to be a major shift into the pro-American worker camp, Trump in September signed a proclamation slapping a $100,000 fee on all new H-1B applications, but opponents of the program have criticized the fee‚Äôs limitations and workarounds. Earlier in November, Trump once again publicly touted the need for H-1Bs to import foreign workers. Unlike many of the tech workers who spoke to the DCNF, he had no problem being identified by his full name. ‚ÄúWhat are they gonna do?‚Äù Ibrahim asked. ‚ÄúThey‚Äôre already not hiring me.‚Äù ‚ÄúYou know, if I went into college and on the pamphlet, there were like, ‚Äòpros and cons of studying something in computer science: you may have to train your replacement at some point in your career,‚Äô I would have never studied this,‚Äù he said. Established by Congress in 1990, the H-1B program was originally intended to utilize ‚Äúhighly specialized‚Äù foreign labor, according to the U.S. Citizenship and Immigration Services. Although it‚Äôs a nonimmigrant visa, H-1B holders can eventually become eligible to apply for legal permanent residence, allowing them to stay in the country indefinitely. The tech industry dominates the use of H-1Bs, with tech companies accounting for nearly 70% of H-1B petitions annually, according to Nation Connections, a site dedicated to helping individuals navigate immigration laws in different countries. Other American-born tech workers have shared similar experiences to Jonathan‚Äôs, and have stayed silent due to fear of retaliation. ‚ÄúI do feel kind of disillusioned with the industry,‚Äù said Riley, who graduated with a software engineering degree in 2021. ‚ÄúSoftware engineers have a higher unemployment rate right now than art history majors.‚Äù Art history majors have a 3% unemployment rate, according to the Federal Reserve Bank of New York, which compiled data released in February. Computer engineering majors, on the other hand, currently suffer from a 7.5% unemployment rate. Riley said he noticed a monumental shift in the hiring practices of an Austin-based company he worked at for several years. He claims the company ‚Äî which had faced consistent complaints from engineers about pay ‚Äî increasingly staffed its engineering departments with employees from South America and eventually established an office in Colombia to better utilize the continent‚Äôs workforce. ‚ÄúI believe that that was done in order to, you know, reduce their labor costs so that they could get engineers without negotiating with [the American-born engineers] or caving to their demands,‚Äù Riley said. Jonathan described a similar situation after the California-based company he worked for introduced an India development center. Roughly six months after the center was launched, he said the company stopped hiring outside of India altogether. About a year after he left, Jonathan‚Äôs former coworker informed him that around half of the company‚Äôs security personnel was let go. ‚ÄúYou‚Äôre going to lose advancement opportunities, you‚Äôre going to have HR problems and you‚Äôre going to be not a team player if you don‚Äôt advocate with open arms the idea of an Indian development center being opened up to your company or a billion H-1Bs flooding the market,‚Äù Jonathan said about the situation he was facing and the continued pressure to not speak out. ‚ÄòWe‚Äôre All In The Process Of Being Replaced‚Äô India stands far above any other nation as the top source of foreign labor, making up 72% of all H-1B recipients between October 2022 and September 2023, per a March 2024 report from the Department of Homeland Security. ‚ÄúWe‚Äôre all in the process of being replaced,‚Äù John, who worked for an insurance company in Connecticut, told the DCNF. John said there were around 350 IT employees ‚Äî all purportedly American ‚Äî at his company when he first began in 2006. Throughout his decade at the company, he claims they were all steadily booted out in favor of foreign workers. ‚ÄúMost of the time they had them train their Indian replacements before they left as a condition of receiving their severance,‚Äù he told the DCNF. ‚ÄúSo what I saw over a period of time was a whole bunch of lives being destroyed.‚Äù ‚ÄúA lot of the younger kids can‚Äôt find employment,‚Äù John said of the industry. ‚ÄúThey spent a whole bunch of money learning all of this stuff ‚Äî computer programs, cloud platforms, this that the other thing ‚Äî but they can‚Äôt find work.‚Äù The tech employees who spoke to the DCNF are struggling to find work in the U.S. at a time when college debt has skyrocketed to historical highs. Roughly 44 million Americans owe more than $1.7 trillion in student debt, according to the National Conference of State Legislatures. Engineering degrees in general are consistently ranked as one of the costliest to earn. Like his coworkers before him, John was ultimately ‚Äúreplaced‚Äù and handed a severance agreement that forbids him from discussing the matter publicly. ‚ÄúComing home to western Washington from Alaska, I assumed that finding a better-paying job would be no issue ‚Äî we are home to some of the nation‚Äôs largest tech companies,‚Äù Luke Hawthorne told the DCNF. ‚ÄúI spent nearly a year over 2022 and 2023 searching for my current job, a job which pays me about the same as I was making before.‚Äù While Hawthorne still considers himself lucky to be employed, he said his current salary ‚Äúdoesn‚Äôt even approach‚Äù the threshold it takes to afford a home in his area of Washington State. His home state‚Äôs software developer workforce grew by more than 16% through H-1B certifications over just a 9-month period, with 83% of these positions approved at or below Washington State‚Äôs median wage, according to public data he analyzed and shared with the DCNF. ‚ÄúThe ‚Äòbest and brightest‚Äô argument simply doesn‚Äôt square with how the program is being used,‚Äù Hawthorne said. ‚ÄúAnother important aspect of it is that you aren‚Äôt competing just with the new arrivals, but with all of the tech workers who have been replaced ‚Äî I have friends with talent and experience who have been out of work for years.‚Äù Many of the tech workers who spoke to the DCNF have since become involved with U.S. Tech Workers, an advocacy group that highlights the plight of American employees negatively affected by the H-1B program and pushes Washington, D.C., for change. Trump, who has implemented some of the most hawkish immigration policies since returning to office, has appeared to give mixed signals on the issue as major players within his own inner circle disagree over reform. The president‚Äôs coalition appeared fragmented in the weeks leading up to his second presidential inauguration, with business magnate Elon Musk touting H-1Bs in December 2024 and Vivek Ramaswamy suggesting that the U.S. needs foreign talent because American culture ‚Äúvenerated mediocrity over excellence.‚Äù Georgia GOP Rep. Marjorie Taylor Greene, a former a top Trump ally who is resigning from Congress, said in November she would introduce legislation completely phasing out the H-1B program, accusing tech companies of abusing the system at the expense of Americans. Trump initially appeared to side with the pro-H-1B faction, declaring in December 2024 that he was ‚Äúa believer‚Äù in the visa program. In what appeared to be a major shift into the pro-American worker camp, Trump in September signed a proclamation slapping a $100,000 fee on all new H-1B applications, but opponents of the program have criticized the fee‚Äôs limitations and workarounds. Earlier in November, Trump once again publicly touted the need for H-1Bs to import foreign workers. As Washington, D.C., continues to debate the value of H-1Bs, American tech workers say they‚Äôve been left out to dry. ‚ÄúI graduated college seven years ago and I remember in high school them telling us, ‚Äòlearn to code and you‚Äôll have a good job,'‚Äù Joseph Ibrahim, an unemployed tech worker based in Florida, told the DCNF. ‚ÄúWell, it turns out they outsource the coding jobs also, not just the manufacturing jobs.‚Äù Ibrahim got a degree in information systems, business analytics and information systems, but has been struggling to find work since April. Unlike many of the tech workers who spoke to the DCNF, he had no problem being identified by his full name. ‚ÄúWhat are they gonna do?‚Äù Ibrahim asked. ‚ÄúThey‚Äôre already not hiring me.‚Äù ‚ÄúYou know, if I went into college and on the pamphlet, there were like, ‚Äòpros and cons of studying something in computer science: you may have to train your replacement at some point in your career,‚Äô I would have never studied this,‚Äù he said. Free Republic Browse ¬∑ Search Bloggers & Personal Topics ¬∑ Post Article FreeRepublic, LLC, PO BOX 9771, FRESNO, CA 93794 FreeRepublic.com is powered by software copyright 2000-2008 John Robinson While H-1Bs have an outsized influence on the tech world, workers across all major industries are impacted by imported foreign labor. The flow of H-1B workers into the U.S. has largely kept apace despite these mass layoffs, with the ISPP finding that the number of H-1B visa workers has grown 80% since the Great Recession low in 2011. Experts estimate that nearly 660,000 H-1B workers were living in the U.S. in October 2024. Established by Congress in 1990, the H-1B program was originally intended to utilize ‚Äúhighly specialized‚Äù foreign labor, according to the U.S. Citizenship and Immigration Services. Although it‚Äôs a nonimmigrant visa, H-1B holders can eventually become eligible to apply for legal permanent residence, allowing them to stay in the country indefinitely. The tech industry dominates the use of H-1Bs, with tech companies accounting for nearly 70% of H-1B petitions annually, according to Nation Connections, a site dedicated to helping individuals navigate immigration laws in different countries. Other American-born tech workers have shared similar experiences to Jonathan‚Äôs, and have stayed silent due to fear of retaliation. ‚ÄúI do feel kind of disillusioned with the industry,‚Äù said Riley, who graduated with a software engineering degree in 2021. ‚ÄúSoftware engineers have a higher unemployment rate right now than art history majors.‚Äù Art history majors have a 3% unemployment rate, according to the Federal Reserve Bank of New York, which compiled data released in February. Computer engineering majors, on the other hand, currently suffer from a 7.5% unemployment rate. Riley said he noticed a monumental shift in the hiring practices of an Austin-based company he worked at for several years. He claims the company ‚Äî which had faced consistent complaints from engineers about pay ‚Äî increasingly staffed its engineering departments with employees from South America and eventually established an office in Colombia to better utilize the continent‚Äôs workforce. ‚ÄúI believe that that was done in order to, you know, reduce their labor costs so that they could get engineers without negotiating with [the American-born engineers] or caving to their demands,‚Äù Riley said. Jonathan described a similar situation after the California-based company he worked for introduced an India development center. Roughly six months after the center was launched, he said the company stopped hiring outside of India altogether. About a year after he left, Jonathan‚Äôs former coworker informed him that around half of the company‚Äôs security personnel was let go. ‚ÄúYou‚Äôre going to lose advancement opportunities, you‚Äôre going to have HR problems and you‚Äôre going to be not a team player if you don‚Äôt advocate with open arms the idea of an Indian development center being opened up to your company or a billion H-1Bs flooding the market,‚Äù Jonathan said about the situation he was facing and the continued pressure to not speak out. ‚ÄòWe‚Äôre All In The Process Of Being Replaced‚Äô India stands far above any other nation as the top source of foreign labor, making up 72% of all H-1B recipients between October 2022 and September 2023, per a March 2024 report from the Department of Homeland Security. ‚ÄúWe‚Äôre all in the process of being replaced,‚Äù John, who worked for an insurance company in Connecticut, told the DCNF. John said there were around 350 IT employees ‚Äî all purportedly American ‚Äî at his company when he first began in 2006. Throughout his decade at the company, he claims they were all steadily booted out in favor of foreign workers. ‚ÄúMost of the time they had them train their Indian replacements before they left as a condition of receiving their severance,‚Äù he told the DCNF. ‚ÄúSo what I saw over a period of time was a whole bunch of lives being destroyed.‚Äù ‚ÄúA lot of the younger kids can‚Äôt find employment,‚Äù John said of the industry. ‚ÄúThey spent a whole bunch of money learning all of this stuff ‚Äî computer programs, cloud platforms, this that the other thing ‚Äî but they can‚Äôt find work.‚Äù The tech employees who spoke to the DCNF are struggling to find work in the U.S. at a time when college debt has skyrocketed to historical highs. Roughly 44 million Americans owe more than $1.7 trillion in student debt, according to the National Conference of State Legislatures. Engineering degrees in general are consistently ranked as one of the costliest to earn. Like his coworkers before him, John was ultimately ‚Äúreplaced‚Äù and handed a severance agreement that forbids him from discussing the matter publicly. ‚ÄúComing home to western Washington from Alaska, I assumed that finding a better-paying job would be no issue ‚Äî we are home to some of the nation‚Äôs largest tech companies,‚Äù Luke Hawthorne told the DCNF. ‚ÄúI spent nearly a year over 2022 and 2023 searching for my current job, a job which pays me about the same as I was making before.‚Äù While Hawthorne still considers himself lucky to be employed, he said his current salary ‚Äúdoesn‚Äôt even approach‚Äù the threshold it takes to afford a home in his area of Washington State. His home state‚Äôs software developer workforce grew by more than 16% through H-1B certifications over just a 9-month period, with 83% of these positions approved at or below Washington State‚Äôs median wage, according to public data he analyzed and shared with the DCNF. ‚ÄúThe ‚Äòbest and brightest‚Äô argument simply doesn‚Äôt square with how the program is being used,‚Äù Hawthorne said. ‚ÄúAnother important aspect of it is that you aren‚Äôt competing just with the new arrivals, but with all of the tech workers who have been replaced ‚Äî I have friends with talent and experience who have been out of work for years.‚Äù Many of the tech workers who spoke to the DCNF have since become involved with U.S. Tech Workers, an advocacy group that highlights the plight of American employees negatively affected by the H-1B program and pushes Washington, D.C., for change. Trump, who has implemented some of the most hawkish immigration policies since returning to office, has appeared to give mixed signals on the issue as major players within his own inner circle disagree over reform. The president‚Äôs coalition appeared fragmented in the weeks leading up to his second presidential inauguration, with business magnate Elon Musk touting H-1Bs in December 2024 and Vivek Ramaswamy suggesting that the U.S. needs foreign talent because American culture ‚Äúvenerated mediocrity over excellence.‚Äù Georgia GOP Rep. Marjorie Taylor Greene, a former a top Trump ally who is resigning from Congress, said in November she would introduce legislation completely phasing out the H-1B program, accusing tech companies of abusing the system at the expense of Americans. Trump initially appeared to side with the pro-H-1B faction, declaring in December 2024 that he was ‚Äúa believer‚Äù in the visa program. In what appeared to be a major shift into the pro-American worker camp, Trump in September signed a proclamation slapping a $100,000 fee on all new H-1B applications, but opponents of the program have criticized the fee‚Äôs limitations and workarounds. Earlier in November, Trump once again publicly touted the need for H-1Bs to import foreign workers. As Washington, D.C., continues to debate the value of H-1Bs, American tech workers say they‚Äôve been left out to dry. ‚ÄúI graduated college seven years ago and I remember in high school them telling us, ‚Äòlearn to code and you‚Äôll have a good job,'‚Äù Joseph Ibrahim, an unemployed tech worker based in Florida, told the DCNF. ‚ÄúWell, it turns out they outsource the coding jobs also, not just the manufacturing jobs.‚Äù Ibrahim got a degree in information systems, business analytics and information systems, but has been struggling to find work since April. Unlike many of the tech workers who spoke to the DCNF, he had no problem being identified by his full name. ‚ÄúWhat are they gonna do?‚Äù Ibrahim asked. ‚ÄúThey‚Äôre already not hiring me.‚Äù ‚ÄúYou know, if I went into college and on the pamphlet, there were like, ‚Äòpros and cons of studying something in computer science: you may have to train your replacement at some point in your career,‚Äô I would have never studied this,‚Äù he said. [ Post Reply | Private Reply | To 3 | View Replies] To: ClearCase_guy The biggest problem with the IT field is that it has two characteristics that make it fertile ground for a "race to the bottom" type of business/employment environment: 1. Like almost any STEM field, it is universal in nature and therefore easily transferable across borders. 2. It doesn't require professional licensure. The second one is a big one, because it's what sets an IT professional apart from, say, a medical doctor, a professional engineer, lawyer, or a CPA. The educational requirements for licensure in some of these fields represent a high barrier to entry for foreigners who might otherwise be qualified to do the work. 12 posted on 12/02/2025 8:57:07 AM PST by Alberta's Child ("There's somebody new and he sure ain't no rodeo man.") [ Post Reply | Private Reply | To 3 | View Replies] To: ClearCase_guy The biggest problem with the IT field is that it has two characteristics that make it fertile ground for a "race to the bottom" type of business/employment environment: 1. Free Republic Browse ¬∑ Search Bloggers & Personal Topics ¬∑ Post Article FreeRepublic, LLC, PO BOX 9771, FRESNO, CA 93794 FreeRepublic.com is powered by software copyright 2000-2008 John Robinson Established by Congress in 1990, the H-1B program was originally intended to utilize ‚Äúhighly specialized‚Äù foreign labor, according to the U.S. Citizenship and Immigration Services. Although it‚Äôs a nonimmigrant visa, H-1B holders can eventually become eligible to apply for legal permanent residence, allowing them to stay in the country indefinitely. The tech industry dominates the use of H-1Bs, with tech companies accounting for nearly 70% of H-1B petitions annually, according to Nation Connections, a site dedicated to helping individuals navigate immigration laws in different countries. Other American-born tech workers have shared similar experiences to Jonathan‚Äôs, and have stayed silent due to fear of retaliation. ‚ÄúI do feel kind of disillusioned with the industry,‚Äù said Riley, who graduated with a software engineering degree in 2021. ‚ÄúSoftware engineers have a higher unemployment rate right now than art history majors.‚Äù Art history majors have a 3% unemployment rate, according to the Federal Reserve Bank of New York, which compiled data released in February. Computer engineering majors, on the other hand, currently suffer from a 7.5% unemployment rate. Riley said he noticed a monumental shift in the hiring practices of an Austin-based company he worked at for several years. He claims the company ‚Äî which had faced consistent complaints from engineers about pay ‚Äî increasingly staffed its engineering departments with employees from South America and eventually established an office in Colombia to better utilize the continent‚Äôs workforce. ‚ÄúI believe that that was done in order to, you know, reduce their labor costs so that they could get engineers without negotiating with [the American-born engineers] or caving to their demands,‚Äù Riley said. Jonathan described a similar situation after the California-based company he worked for introduced an India development center. Roughly six months after the center was launched, he said the company stopped hiring outside of India altogether. About a year after he left, Jonathan‚Äôs former coworker informed him that around half of the company‚Äôs security personnel was let go. ‚ÄúYou‚Äôre going to lose advancement opportunities, you‚Äôre going to have HR problems and you‚Äôre going to be not a team player if you don‚Äôt advocate with open arms the idea of an Indian development center being opened up to your company or a billion H-1Bs flooding the market,‚Äù Jonathan said about the situation he was facing and the continued pressure to not speak out. ‚ÄòWe‚Äôre All In The Process Of Being Replaced‚Äô India stands far above any other nation as the top source of foreign labor, making up 72% of all H-1B recipients between October 2022 and September 2023, per a March 2024 report from the Department of Homeland Security. ‚ÄúWe‚Äôre all in the process of being replaced,‚Äù John, who worked for an insurance company in Connecticut, told the DCNF. John said there were around 350 IT employees ‚Äî all purportedly American ‚Äî at his company when he first began in 2006. Throughout his decade at the company, he claims they were all steadily booted out in favor of foreign workers. ‚ÄúMost of the time they had them train their Indian replacements before they left as a condition of receiving their severance,‚Äù he told the DCNF. ‚ÄúSo what I saw over a period of time was a whole bunch of lives being destroyed.‚Äù ‚ÄúA lot of the younger kids can‚Äôt find employment,‚Äù John said of the industry. ‚ÄúThey spent a whole bunch of money learning all of this stuff ‚Äî computer programs, cloud platforms, this that the other thing ‚Äî but they can‚Äôt find work.‚Äù The tech employees who spoke to the DCNF are struggling to find work in the U.S. at a time when college debt has skyrocketed to historical highs. Roughly 44 million Americans owe more than $1.7 trillion in student debt, according to the National Conference of State Legislatures. Engineering degrees in general are consistently ranked as one of the costliest to earn. Like his coworkers before him, John was ultimately ‚Äúreplaced‚Äù and handed a severance agreement that forbids him from discussing the matter publicly. ‚ÄúComing home to western Washington from Alaska, I assumed that finding a better-paying job would be no issue ‚Äî we are home to some of the nation‚Äôs largest tech companies,‚Äù Luke Hawthorne told the DCNF. ‚ÄúI spent nearly a year over 2022 and 2023 searching for my current job, a job which pays me about the same as I was making before.‚Äù While Hawthorne still considers himself lucky to be employed, he said his current salary ‚Äúdoesn‚Äôt even approach‚Äù the threshold it takes to afford a home in his area of Washington State. His home state‚Äôs software developer workforce grew by more than 16% through H-1B certifications over just a 9-month period, with 83% of these positions approved at or below Washington State‚Äôs median wage, according to public data he analyzed and shared with the DCNF. ‚ÄúThe ‚Äòbest and brightest‚Äô argument simply doesn‚Äôt square with how the program is being used,‚Äù Hawthorne said. ‚ÄúAnother important aspect of it is that you aren‚Äôt competing just with the new arrivals, but with all of the tech workers who have been replaced ‚Äî I have friends with talent and experience who have been out of work for years.‚Äù Many of the tech workers who spoke to the DCNF have since become involved with U.S. Tech Workers, an advocacy group that highlights the plight of American employees negatively affected by the H-1B program and pushes Washington, D.C., for change. Trump, who has implemented some of the most hawkish immigration policies since returning to office, has appeared to give mixed signals on the issue as major players within his own inner circle disagree over reform. The president‚Äôs coalition appeared fragmented in the weeks leading up to his second presidential inauguration, with business magnate Elon Musk touting H-1Bs in December 2024 and Vivek Ramaswamy suggesting that the U.S. needs foreign talent because American culture ‚Äúvenerated mediocrity over excellence.‚Äù Georgia GOP Rep. Marjorie Taylor Greene, a former a top Trump ally who is resigning from Congress, said in November she would introduce legislation completely phasing out the H-1B program, accusing tech companies of abusing the system at the expense of Americans. Trump initially appeared to side with the pro-H-1B faction, declaring in December 2024 that he was ‚Äúa believer‚Äù in the visa program. In what appeared to be a major shift into the pro-American worker camp, Trump in September signed a proclamation slapping a $100,000 fee on all new H-1B applications, but opponents of the program have criticized the fee‚Äôs limitations and workarounds. Earlier in November, Trump once again publicly touted the need for H-1Bs to import foreign workers. As Washington, D.C., continues to debate the value of H-1Bs, American tech workers say they‚Äôve been left out to dry. ‚ÄúI graduated college seven years ago and I remember in high school them telling us, ‚Äòlearn to code and you‚Äôll have a good job,'‚Äù Joseph Ibrahim, an unemployed tech worker based in Florida, told the DCNF. ‚ÄúWell, it turns out they outsource the coding jobs also, not just the manufacturing jobs.‚Äù Ibrahim got a degree in information systems, business analytics and information systems, but has been struggling to find work since April. Unlike many of the tech workers who spoke to the DCNF, he had no problem being identified by his full name. ‚ÄúWhat are they gonna do?‚Äù Ibrahim asked. ‚ÄúThey‚Äôre already not hiring me.‚Äù ‚ÄúYou know, if I went into college and on the pamphlet, there were like, ‚Äòpros and cons of studying something in computer science: you may have to train your replacement at some point in your career,‚Äô I would have never studied this,‚Äù he said. [ Post Reply | Private Reply | To 3 | View Replies] To: ClearCase_guy The biggest problem with the IT field is that it has two characteristics that make it fertile ground for a "race to the bottom" type of business/employment environment: 1. Like almost any STEM field, it is universal in nature and therefore easily transferable across borders. 2. It doesn't require professional licensure. The second one is a big one, because it's what sets an IT professional apart from, say, a medical doctor, a professional engineer, lawyer, or a CPA. The educational requirements for licensure in some of these fields represent a high barrier to entry for foreigners who might otherwise be qualified to do the work. 12 posted on 12/02/2025 8:57:07 AM PST by Alberta's Child ("There's somebody new and he sure ain't no rodeo man.") Computer engineering majors, on the other hand, currently suffer from a 7.5% unemployment rate. Riley said he noticed a monumental shift in the hiring practices of an Austin-based company he worked at for several years. He claims the company ‚Äî which had faced consistent complaints from engineers about pay ‚Äî increasingly staffed its engineering departments with employees from South America and eventually established an office in Colombia to better utilize the continent‚Äôs workforce. ‚ÄúI believe that that was done in order to, you know, reduce their labor costs so that they could get engineers without negotiating with [the American-born engineers] or caving to their demands,‚Äù Riley said. Jonathan described a similar situation after the California-based company he worked for introduced an India development center. Roughly six months after the center was launched, he said the company stopped hiring outside of India altogether. About a year after he left, Jonathan‚Äôs former coworker informed him that around half of the company‚Äôs security personnel was let go. ‚ÄúYou‚Äôre going to lose advancement opportunities, you‚Äôre going to have HR problems and you‚Äôre going to be not a team player if you don‚Äôt advocate with open arms the idea of an Indian development center being opened up to your company or a billion H-1Bs flooding the market,‚Äù Jonathan said about the situation he was facing and the continued pressure to not speak out. ‚ÄòWe‚Äôre All In The Process Of Being Replaced‚Äô India stands far above any other nation as the top source of foreign labor, making up 72% of all H-1B recipients between October 2022 and September 2023, per a March 2024 report from the Department of Homeland Security. ‚ÄúWe‚Äôre all in the process of being replaced,‚Äù John, who worked for an insurance company in Connecticut, told the DCNF. John said there were around 350 IT employees ‚Äî all purportedly American ‚Äî at his company when he first began in 2006. Throughout his decade at the company, he claims they were all steadily booted out in favor of foreign workers. ‚ÄúMost of the time they had them train their Indian replacements before they left as a condition of receiving their severance,‚Äù he told the DCNF. ‚ÄúSo what I saw over a period of time was a whole bunch of lives being destroyed.‚Äù ‚ÄúA lot of the younger kids can‚Äôt find employment,‚Äù John said of the industry. ‚ÄúThey spent a whole bunch of money learning all of this stuff ‚Äî computer programs, cloud platforms, this that the other thing ‚Äî but they can‚Äôt find work.‚Äù The tech employees who spoke to the DCNF are struggling to find work in the U.S. at a time when college debt has skyrocketed to historical highs. Roughly 44 million Americans owe more than $1.7 trillion in student debt, according to the National Conference of State Legislatures. Engineering degrees in general are consistently ranked as one of the costliest to earn. Like his coworkers before him, John was ultimately ‚Äúreplaced‚Äù and handed a severance agreement that forbids him from discussing the matter publicly. ‚ÄúComing home to western Washington from Alaska, I assumed that finding a better-paying job would be no issue ‚Äî we are home to some of the nation‚Äôs largest tech companies,‚Äù Luke Hawthorne told the DCNF. ‚ÄúI spent nearly a year over 2022 and 2023 searching for my current job, a job which pays me about the same as I was making before.‚Äù While Hawthorne still considers himself lucky to be employed, he said his current salary ‚Äúdoesn‚Äôt even approach‚Äù the threshold it takes to afford a home in his area of Washington State. His home state‚Äôs software developer workforce grew by more than 16% through H-1B certifications over just a 9-month period, with 83% of these positions approved at or below Washington State‚Äôs median wage, according to public data he analyzed and shared with the DCNF. ‚ÄúThe ‚Äòbest and brightest‚Äô argument simply doesn‚Äôt square with how the program is being used,‚Äù Hawthorne said. ‚ÄúAnother important aspect of it is that you aren‚Äôt competing just with the new arrivals, but with all of the tech workers who have been replaced ‚Äî I have friends with talent and experience who have been out of work for years.‚Äù Many of the tech workers who spoke to the DCNF have since become involved with U.S. Tech Workers, an advocacy group that highlights the plight of American employees negatively affected by the H-1B program and pushes Washington, D.C., for change. Trump, who has implemented some of the most hawkish immigration policies since returning to office, has appeared to give mixed signals on the issue as major players within his own inner circle disagree over reform. The president‚Äôs coalition appeared fragmented in the weeks leading up to his second presidential inauguration, with business magnate Elon Musk touting H-1Bs in December 2024 and Vivek Ramaswamy suggesting that the U.S. needs foreign talent because American culture ‚Äúvenerated mediocrity over excellence.‚Äù Georgia GOP Rep. Marjorie Taylor Greene, a former a top Trump ally who is resigning from Congress, said in November she would introduce legislation completely phasing out the H-1B program, accusing tech companies of abusing the system at the expense of Americans. Trump initially appeared to side with the pro-H-1B faction, declaring in December 2024 that he was ‚Äúa believer‚Äù in the visa program. In what appeared to be a major shift into the pro-American worker camp, Trump in September signed a proclamation slapping a $100,000 fee on all new H-1B applications, but opponents of the program have criticized the fee‚Äôs limitations and workarounds. Earlier in November, Trump once again publicly touted the need for H-1Bs to import foreign workers. As Washington, D.C., continues to debate the value of H-1Bs, American tech workers say they‚Äôve been left out to dry. ‚ÄúI graduated college seven years ago and I remember in high school them telling us, ‚Äòlearn to code and you‚Äôll have a good job,'‚Äù Joseph Ibrahim, an unemployed tech worker based in Florida, told the DCNF. ‚ÄúWell, it turns out they outsource the coding jobs also, not just the manufacturing jobs.‚Äù Ibrahim got a degree in information systems, business analytics and information systems, but has been struggling to find work since April. His home state‚Äôs software developer workforce grew by more than 16% through H-1B certifications over just a 9-month period, with 83% of these positions approved at or below Washington State‚Äôs median wage, according to public data he analyzed and shared with the DCNF. ‚ÄúThe ‚Äòbest and brightest‚Äô argument simply doesn‚Äôt square with how the program is being used,‚Äù Hawthorne said. ‚ÄúAnother important aspect of it is that you aren‚Äôt competing just with the new arrivals, but with all of the tech workers who have been replaced ‚Äî I have friends with talent and experience who have been out of work for years.‚Äù Many of the tech workers who spoke to the DCNF have since become involved with U.S. Tech Workers, an advocacy group that highlights the plight of American employees negatively affected by the H-1B program and pushes Washington, D.C., for change. Trump, who has implemented some of the most hawkish immigration policies since returning to office, has appeared to give mixed signals on the issue as major players within his own inner circle disagree over reform. The president‚Äôs coalition appeared fragmented in the weeks leading up to his second presidential inauguration, with business magnate Elon Musk touting H-1Bs in December 2024 and Vivek Ramaswamy suggesting that the U.S. needs foreign talent because American culture ‚Äúvenerated mediocrity over excellence.‚Äù Georgia GOP Rep. Marjorie Taylor Greene, a former a top Trump ally who is resigning from Congress, said in November she would introduce legislation completely phasing out the H-1B program, accusing tech companies of abusing the system at the expense of Americans. Trump initially appeared to side with the pro-H-1B faction, declaring in December 2024 that he was ‚Äúa believer‚Äù in the visa program. In what appeared to be a major shift into the pro-American worker camp, Trump in September signed a proclamation slapping a $100,000 fee on all new H-1B applications, but opponents of the program have criticized the fee‚Äôs limitations and workarounds. Earlier in November, Trump once again publicly touted the need for H-1Bs to import foreign workers. As Washington, D.C., continues to debate the value of H-1Bs, American tech workers say they‚Äôve been left out to dry. ‚ÄúI graduated college seven years ago and I remember in high school them telling us, ‚Äòlearn to code and you‚Äôll have a good job,'‚Äù Joseph Ibrahim, an unemployed tech worker based in Florida, told the DCNF. ‚ÄúWell, it turns out they outsource the coding jobs also, not just the manufacturing jobs.‚Äù Ibrahim got a degree in information systems, business analytics and information systems, but has been struggling to find work since April. Unlike many of the tech workers who spoke to the DCNF, he had no problem being identified by his full name. ‚ÄúWhat are they gonna do?‚Äù Ibrahim asked. ‚ÄúThey‚Äôre already not hiring me.‚Äù ‚ÄúYou know, if I went into college and on the pamphlet, there were like, ‚Äòpros and cons of studying something in computer science: you may have to train your replacement at some point in your career,‚Äô I would have never studied this,‚Äù he said. [ Post Reply | Private Reply | To 3 | View Replies] To: ClearCase_guy The biggest problem with the IT field is that it has two characteristics that make it fertile ground for a "race to the bottom" type of business/employment environment: 1. Like almost any STEM field, it is universal in nature and therefore easily transferable across borders. 2. It doesn't require professional licensure. The second one is a big one, because it's what sets an IT professional apart from, say, a medical doctor, a professional engineer, lawyer, or a CPA. The educational requirements for licensure in some of these fields represent a high barrier to entry for foreigners who might otherwise be qualified to do the work. 12 posted on 12/02/2025 8:57:07 AM PST by Alberta's Child ("There's somebody new and he sure ain't no rodeo man.") Throughout his decade at the company, he claims they were all steadily booted out in favor of foreign workers. ‚ÄúMost of the time they had them train their Indian replacements before they left as a condition of receiving their severance,‚Äù he told the DCNF. ‚ÄúSo what I saw over a period of time was a whole bunch of lives being destroyed.‚Äù ‚ÄúA lot of the younger kids can‚Äôt find employment,‚Äù John said of the industry. ‚ÄúThey spent a whole bunch of money learning all of this stuff ‚Äî computer programs, cloud platforms, this that the other thing ‚Äî but they can‚Äôt find work.‚Äù The tech employees who spoke to the DCNF are struggling to find work in the U.S. at a time when college debt has skyrocketed to historical highs. Roughly 44 million Americans owe more than $1.7 trillion in student debt, according to the National Conference of State Legislatures. Engineering degrees in general are consistently ranked as one of the costliest to earn. Like his coworkers before him, John was ultimately ‚Äúreplaced‚Äù and handed a severance agreement that forbids him from discussing the matter publicly. ‚ÄúComing home to western Washington from Alaska, I assumed that finding a better-paying job would be no issue ‚Äî we are home to some of the nation‚Äôs largest tech companies,‚Äù Luke Hawthorne told the DCNF. ‚ÄúI spent nearly a year over 2022 and 2023 searching for my current job, a job which pays me about the same as I was making before.‚Äù While Hawthorne still considers himself lucky to be employed, he said his current salary ‚Äúdoesn‚Äôt even approach‚Äù the threshold it takes to afford a home in his area of Washington State. His home state‚Äôs software developer workforce grew by more than 16% through H-1B certifications over just a 9-month period, with 83% of these positions approved at or below Washington State‚Äôs median wage, according to public data he analyzed and shared with the DCNF. ‚ÄúThe ‚Äòbest and brightest‚Äô argument simply doesn‚Äôt square with how the program is being used,‚Äù Hawthorne said. ‚ÄúAnother important aspect of it is that you aren‚Äôt competing just with the new arrivals, but with all of the tech workers who have been replaced ‚Äî I have friends with talent and experience who have been out of work for years.‚Äù Many of the tech workers who spoke to the DCNF have since become involved with U.S. Tech Workers, an advocacy group that highlights the plight of American employees negatively affected by the H-1B program and pushes Washington, D.C., for change. Trump, who has implemented some of the most hawkish immigration policies since returning to office, has appeared to give mixed signals on the issue as major players within his own inner circle disagree over reform. The president‚Äôs coalition appeared fragmented in the weeks leading up to his second presidential inauguration, with business magnate Elon Musk touting H-1Bs in December 2024 and Vivek Ramaswamy suggesting that the U.S. needs foreign talent because American culture ‚Äúvenerated mediocrity over excellence.‚Äù Georgia GOP Rep. Marjorie Taylor Greene, a former a top Trump ally who is resigning from Congress, said in November she would introduce legislation completely phasing out the H-1B program, accusing tech companies of abusing the system at the expense of Americans. Trump initially appeared to side with the pro-H-1B faction, declaring in December 2024 that he was ‚Äúa believer‚Äù in the visa program. In what appeared to be a major shift into the pro-American worker camp, Trump in September signed a proclamation slapping a $100,000 fee on all new H-1B applications, but opponents of the program have criticized the fee‚Äôs limitations and workarounds. Earlier in November, Trump once again publicly touted the need for H-1Bs to import foreign workers. As Washington, D.C., continues to debate the value of H-1Bs, American tech workers say they‚Äôve been left out to dry. ‚ÄúI graduated college seven years ago and I remember in high school them telling us, ‚Äòlearn to code and you‚Äôll have a good job,'‚Äù Joseph Ibrahim, an unemployed tech worker based in Florida, told the DCNF. ‚ÄúWell, it turns out they outsource the coding jobs also, not just the manufacturing jobs.‚Äù Ibrahim got a degree in information systems, business analytics and information systems, but has been struggling to find work since April. Unlike many of the tech workers who spoke to the DCNF, he had no problem being identified by his full name. ‚ÄúWhat are they gonna do?‚Äù Ibrahim asked. ‚ÄúThey‚Äôre already not hiring me.‚Äù ‚ÄúYou know, if I went into college and on the pamphlet, there were like, ‚Äòpros and cons of studying something in computer science: you may have to train your replacement at some point in your career,‚Äô I would have never studied this,‚Äù he said. [ Post Reply | Private Reply | To 3 | View Replies] To: ClearCase_guy The biggest problem with the IT field is that it has two characteristics that make it fertile ground for a "race to the bottom" type of business/employment environment: 1. Like almost any STEM field, it is universal in nature and therefore easily transferable across borders. 2. It doesn't require professional licensure. The second one is a big one, because it's what sets an IT professional apart from, say, a medical doctor, a professional engineer, lawyer, or a CPA. The educational requirements for licensure in some of these fields represent a high barrier to entry for foreigners who might otherwise be qualified to do the work. 12 posted on 12/02/2025 8:57:07 AM PST by Alberta's Child ("There's somebody new and he sure ain't no rodeo man.") About a year after he left, Jonathan‚Äôs former coworker informed him that around half of the company‚Äôs security personnel was let go. ‚ÄúYou‚Äôre going to lose advancement opportunities, you‚Äôre going to have HR problems and you‚Äôre going to be not a team player if you don‚Äôt advocate with open arms the idea of an Indian development center being opened up to your company or a billion H-1Bs flooding the market,‚Äù Jonathan said about the situation he was facing and the continued pressure to not speak out. ‚ÄòWe‚Äôre All In The Process Of Being Replaced‚Äô India stands far above any other nation as the top source of foreign labor, making up 72% of all H-1B recipients between October 2022 and September 2023, per a March 2024 report from the Department of Homeland Security. ‚ÄúWe‚Äôre all in the process of being replaced,‚Äù John, who worked for an insurance company in Connecticut, told the DCNF. John said there were around 350 IT employees ‚Äî all purportedly American ‚Äî at his company when he first began in 2006. Throughout his decade at the company, he claims they were all steadily booted out in favor of foreign workers. ‚ÄúMost of the time they had them train their Indian replacements before they left as a condition of receiving their severance,‚Äù he told the DCNF. ‚ÄúSo what I saw over a period of time was a whole bunch of lives being destroyed.‚Äù ‚ÄúA lot of the younger kids can‚Äôt find employment,‚Äù John said of the industry. ‚ÄúThey spent a whole bunch of money learning all of this stuff ‚Äî computer programs, cloud platforms, this that the other thing ‚Äî but they can‚Äôt find work.‚Äù The tech employees who spoke to the DCNF are struggling to find work in the U.S. at a time when college debt has skyrocketed to historical highs. Roughly 44 million Americans owe more than $1.7 trillion in student debt, according to the National Conference of State Legislatures. Engineering degrees in general are consistently ranked as one of the costliest to earn. Like his coworkers before him, John was ultimately ‚Äúreplaced‚Äù and handed a severance agreement that forbids him from discussing the matter publicly. ‚ÄúComing home to western Washington from Alaska, I assumed that finding a better-paying job would be no issue ‚Äî we are home to some of the nation‚Äôs largest tech companies,‚Äù Luke Hawthorne told the DCNF. ‚ÄúI spent nearly a year over 2022 and 2023 searching for my current job, a job which pays me about the same as I was making before.‚Äù While Hawthorne still considers himself lucky to be employed, he said his current salary ‚Äúdoesn‚Äôt even approach‚Äù the threshold it takes to afford a home in his area of Washington State. His home state‚Äôs software developer workforce grew by more than 16% through H-1B certifications over just a 9-month period, with 83% of these positions approved at or below Washington State‚Äôs median wage, according to public data he analyzed and shared with the DCNF. ‚ÄúThe ‚Äòbest and brightest‚Äô argument simply doesn‚Äôt square with how the program is being used,‚Äù Hawthorne said. ‚ÄúAnother important aspect of it is that you aren‚Äôt competing just with the new arrivals, but with all of the tech workers who have been replaced ‚Äî I have friends with talent and experience who have been out of work for years.‚Äù Many of the tech workers who spoke to the DCNF have since become involved with U.S. Tech Workers, an advocacy group that highlights the plight of American employees negatively affected by the H-1B program and pushes Washington, D.C., for change. Trump, who has implemented some of the most hawkish immigration policies since returning to office, has appeared to give mixed signals on the issue as major players within his own inner circle disagree over reform. The president‚Äôs coalition appeared fragmented in the weeks leading up to his second presidential inauguration, with business magnate Elon Musk touting H-1Bs in December 2024 and Vivek Ramaswamy suggesting that the U.S. needs foreign talent because American culture ‚Äúvenerated mediocrity over excellence.‚Äù Georgia GOP Rep. Marjorie Taylor Greene, a former a top Trump ally who is resigning from Congress, said in November she would introduce legislation completely phasing out the H-1B program, accusing tech companies of abusing the system at the expense of Americans. Trump initially appeared to side with the pro-H-1B faction, declaring in December 2024 that he was ‚Äúa believer‚Äù in the visa program. In what appeared to be a major shift into the pro-American worker camp, Trump in September signed a proclamation slapping a $100,000 fee on all new H-1B applications, but opponents of the program have criticized the fee‚Äôs limitations and workarounds. Earlier in November, Trump once again publicly touted the need for H-1Bs to import foreign workers. As Washington, D.C., continues to debate the value of H-1Bs, American tech workers say they‚Äôve been left out to dry. ‚ÄúI graduated college seven years ago and I remember in high school them telling us, ‚Äòlearn to code and you‚Äôll have a good job,'‚Äù Joseph Ibrahim, an unemployed tech worker based in Florida, told the DCNF. ‚ÄúWell, it turns out they outsource the coding jobs also, not just the manufacturing jobs.‚Äù Ibrahim got a degree in information systems, business analytics and information systems, but has been struggling to find work since April. Unlike many of the tech workers who spoke to the DCNF, he had no problem being identified by his full name. ‚ÄúWhat are they gonna do?‚Äù Ibrahim asked. ‚ÄúThey‚Äôre already not hiring me.‚Äù ‚ÄúYou know, if I went into college and on the pamphlet, there were like, ‚Äòpros and cons of studying something in computer science: you may have to train your replacement at some point in your career,‚Äô I would have never studied this,‚Äù he said. [ Post Reply | Private Reply | To 3 | View Replies] To: ClearCase_guy The biggest problem with the IT field is that it has two characteristics that make it fertile ground for a "race to the bottom" type of business/employment environment: 1. Like almost any STEM field, it is universal in nature and therefore easily transferable across borders. 2. It doesn't require professional licensure. The second one is a big one, because it's what sets an IT professional apart from, say, a medical doctor, a professional engineer, lawyer, or a CPA. The educational requirements for licensure in some of these fields represent a high barrier to entry for foreigners who might otherwise be qualified to do the work. 12 posted on 12/02/2025 8:57:07 AM PST by Alberta's Child ("There's somebody new and he sure ain't no rodeo man.") Throughout his decade at the company, he claims they were all steadily booted out in favor of foreign workers. ‚ÄúMost of the time they had them train their Indian replacements before they left as a condition of receiving their severance,‚Äù he told the DCNF. ‚ÄúSo what I saw over a period of time was a whole bunch of lives being destroyed.‚Äù ‚ÄúA lot of the younger kids can‚Äôt find employment,‚Äù John said of the industry. ‚ÄúThey spent a whole bunch of money learning all of this stuff ‚Äî computer programs, cloud platforms, this that the other thing ‚Äî but they can‚Äôt find work.‚Äù The tech employees who spoke to the DCNF are struggling to find work in the U.S. at a time when college debt has skyrocketed to historical highs. Roughly 44 million Americans owe more than $1.7 trillion in student debt, according to the National Conference of State Legislatures. Engineering degrees in general are consistently ranked as one of the costliest to earn. Like his coworkers before him, John was ultimately ‚Äúreplaced‚Äù and handed a severance agreement that forbids him from discussing the matter publicly. ‚ÄúComing home to western Washington from Alaska, I assumed that finding a better-paying job would be no issue ‚Äî we are home to some of the nation‚Äôs largest tech companies,‚Äù Luke Hawthorne told the DCNF. ‚ÄúI spent nearly a year over 2022 and 2023 searching for my current job, a job which pays me about the same as I was making before.‚Äù While Hawthorne still considers himself lucky to be employed, he said his current salary ‚Äúdoesn‚Äôt even approach‚Äù the threshold it takes to afford a home in his area of Washington State. His home state‚Äôs software developer workforce grew by more than 16% through H-1B certifications over just a 9-month period, with 83% of these positions approved at or below Washington State‚Äôs median wage, according to public data he analyzed and shared with the DCNF. ‚ÄúThe ‚Äòbest and brightest‚Äô argument simply doesn‚Äôt square with how the program is being used,‚Äù Hawthorne said. ‚ÄúAnother important aspect of it is that you aren‚Äôt competing just with the new arrivals, but with all of the tech workers who have been replaced ‚Äî I have friends with talent and experience who have been out of work for years.‚Äù Many of the tech workers who spoke to the DCNF have since become involved with U.S. Tech Workers, an advocacy group that highlights the plight of American employees negatively affected by the H-1B program and pushes Washington, D.C., for change. Trump, who has implemented some of the most hawkish immigration policies since returning to office, has appeared to give mixed signals on the issue as major players within his own inner circle disagree over reform. The president‚Äôs coalition appeared fragmented in the weeks leading up to his second presidential inauguration, with business magnate Elon Musk touting H-1Bs in December 2024 and Vivek Ramaswamy suggesting that the U.S. needs foreign talent because American culture ‚Äúvenerated mediocrity over excellence.‚Äù Georgia GOP Rep. Marjorie Taylor Greene, a former a top Trump ally who is resigning from Congress, said in November she would introduce legislation completely phasing out the H-1B program, accusing tech companies of abusing the system at the expense of Americans. Trump initially appeared to side with the pro-H-1B faction, declaring in December 2024 that he was ‚Äúa believer‚Äù in the visa program. In what appeared to be a major shift into the pro-American worker camp, Trump in September signed a proclamation slapping a $100,000 fee on all new H-1B applications, but opponents of the program have criticized the fee‚Äôs limitations and workarounds. Earlier in November, Trump once again publicly touted the need for H-1Bs to import foreign workers. As Washington, D.C., continues to debate the value of H-1Bs, American tech workers say they‚Äôve been left out to dry. ‚ÄúI graduated college seven years ago and I remember in high school them telling us, ‚Äòlearn to code and you‚Äôll have a good job,'‚Äù Joseph Ibrahim, an unemployed tech worker based in Florida, told the DCNF. ‚ÄúWell, it turns out they outsource the coding jobs also, not just the manufacturing jobs.‚Äù Ibrahim got a degree in information systems, business analytics and information systems, but has been struggling to find work since April. Unlike many of the tech workers who spoke to the DCNF, he had no problem being identified by his full name. ‚ÄúWhat are they gonna do?‚Äù Ibrahim asked. ‚ÄúThey‚Äôre already not hiring me.‚Äù ‚ÄúYou know, if I went into college and on the pamphlet, there were like, ‚Äòpros and cons of studying something in computer science: you may have to train your replacement at some point in your career,‚Äô I would have never studied this,‚Äù he said. [ Post Reply | Private Reply | To 3 | View Replies] To: ClearCase_guy The biggest problem with the IT field is that it has two characteristics that make it fertile ground for a "race to the bottom" type of business/employment environment: 1. Like almost any STEM field, it is universal in nature and therefore easily transferable across borders. 2. It doesn't require professional licensure. The second one is a big one, because it's what sets an IT professional apart from, say, a medical doctor, a professional engineer, lawyer, or a CPA. The educational requirements for licensure in some of these fields represent a high barrier to entry for foreigners who might otherwise be qualified to do the work. 12 posted on 12/02/2025 8:57:07 AM PST by Alberta's Child ("There's somebody new and he sure ain't no rodeo man.") His home state‚Äôs software developer workforce grew by more than 16% through H-1B certifications over just a 9-month period, with 83% of these positions approved at or below Washington State‚Äôs median wage, according to public data he analyzed and shared with the DCNF. ‚ÄúThe ‚Äòbest and brightest‚Äô argument simply doesn‚Äôt square with how the program is being used,‚Äù Hawthorne said. ‚ÄúAnother important aspect of it is that you aren‚Äôt competing just with the new arrivals, but with all of the tech workers who have been replaced ‚Äî I have friends with talent and experience who have been out of work for years.‚Äù Many of the tech workers who spoke to the DCNF have since become involved with U.S. Tech Workers, an advocacy group that highlights the plight of American employees negatively affected by the H-1B program and pushes Washington, D.C., for change. Trump, who has implemented some of the most hawkish immigration policies since returning to office, has appeared to give mixed signals on the issue as major players within his own inner circle disagree over reform. The president‚Äôs coalition appeared fragmented in the weeks leading up to his second presidential inauguration, with business magnate Elon Musk touting H-1Bs in December 2024 and Vivek Ramaswamy suggesting that the U.S. needs foreign talent because American culture ‚Äúvenerated mediocrity over excellence.‚Äù Georgia GOP Rep. Marjorie Taylor Greene, a former a top Trump ally who is resigning from Congress, said in November she would introduce legislation completely phasing out the H-1B program, accusing tech companies of abusing the system at the expense of Americans. Trump initially appeared to side with the pro-H-1B faction, declaring in December 2024 that he was ‚Äúa believer‚Äù in the visa program. In what appeared to be a major shift into the pro-American worker camp, Trump in September signed a proclamation slapping a $100,000 fee on all new H-1B applications, but opponents of the program have criticized the fee‚Äôs limitations and workarounds. Earlier in November, Trump once again publicly touted the need for H-1Bs to import foreign workers. As Washington, D.C., continues to debate the value of H-1Bs, American tech workers say they‚Äôve been left out to dry. ‚ÄúI graduated college seven years ago and I remember in high school them telling us, ‚Äòlearn to code and you‚Äôll have a good job,'‚Äù Joseph Ibrahim, an unemployed tech worker based in Florida, told the DCNF. ‚ÄúWell, it turns out they outsource the coding jobs also, not just the manufacturing jobs.‚Äù Ibrahim got a degree in information systems, business analytics and information systems, but has been struggling to find work since April. Unlike many of the tech workers who spoke to the DCNF, he had no problem being identified by his full name. ‚ÄúWhat are they gonna do?‚Äù Ibrahim asked. ‚ÄúThey‚Äôre already not hiring me.‚Äù ‚ÄúYou know, if I went into college and on the pamphlet, there were like, ‚Äòpros and cons of studying something in computer science: you may have to train your replacement at some point in your career,‚Äô I would have never studied this,‚Äù he said. [ Post Reply | Private Reply | To 3 | View Replies] To: ClearCase_guy The biggest problem with the IT field is that it has two characteristics that make it fertile ground for a "race to the bottom" type of business/employment environment: 1. Like almost any STEM field, it is universal in nature and therefore easily transferable across borders. 2. It doesn't require professional licensure. The second one is a big one, because it's what sets an IT professional apart from, say, a medical doctor, a professional engineer, lawyer, or a CPA. The educational requirements for licensure in some of these fields represent a high barrier to entry for foreigners who might otherwise be qualified to do the work. 12 posted on 12/02/2025 8:57:07 AM PST by Alberta's Child ("There's somebody new and he sure ain't no rodeo man.") [ Post Reply | Private Reply | To 3 | View Replies] To: ClearCase_guy The biggest problem with the IT field is that it has two characteristics that make it fertile ground for a "race to the bottom" type of business/employment environment: 1. The second one is a big one, because it's what sets an IT professional apart from, say, a medical doctor, a professional engineer, lawyer, or a CPA. The educational requirements for licensure in some of these fields represent a high barrier to entry for foreigners who might otherwise be qualified to do the work. 12 posted on 12/02/2025 8:57:07 AM PST by Alberta's Child ("There's somebody new and he sure ain't no rodeo man.")
